=245  \\$aRembrandt van Rijn$b[Algemeen Handelsblad, 1852]
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bDrukkerij van het Algemeen Handelsblad$c1852
=300  \\$a6 pages$billustrations
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aNewspaper extract of the Algemeen Handelsblad of 28 mai 1852 (an influential Amsterdam-based liberal daily newspaper published between 1828 and 1970), on the occasion of King Willem III unveiling in 1852 a cast-iron Rembrandt monument designed by Louis Royer on the Amsterdam Botermarkt-square (named Rembrandtplein since 1876). 
=500  \\$a4 pages Biography, ending with poem by Thijm, plus 2 pages text that appeared on the title page of the Newspaper.
=500  \\$aThe biography ends with a long celebrating poem on Rembrandt by J.A. Alberdingk Thijm (1820-1889) titled "Een Harptoon in het Akkoord der Rembrandtshulde"
https://www.dbnl.org/tekst/albe003voor01_01/albe003voor01_01_0016.php

=041  \\$ager
=245  \\$aUnter Allerhöchster Autoriteit Ihro Kön. Maj. zu Dännemark, Norwegen u. Schleswig-Holsteinische Anzeigen 40stes Stück. Montag den 7ten October 1799
=260  \\$as.l.$bs.n.$c1799
=300  \\$a4 pages$bquadruple-folded pages$c42x36c cm
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aThe Schleswig-Holsteinische Anzeigen (SchlHA) is the justice journal of the German federal state of Schleswig-Holstein and at the same time one of the oldest periodicals of the state.
The Schleswig-Holsteinische Anzeigen date back to the time of the duchies of Schleswig and Holstein and have been published since 1750.[1] They are an announcement journal that was published under the same title by both the kings of Denmark and the diverse rulers in Schleswig-Holstein such as the House of Schleswig-Holstein-Gottorf. Today, the publisher is the state's Ministry of Justice, which has left the editorship to the Higher Regional Court of Schleswig. They are divided into a monthly Part A (with the editorial content of a legal journal and contributions on case law in the judicial district of the state's only Higher Regional Court) and a twice-monthly Part B (advertising section and judicial notices). It is therefore an official journal and not an advertising journal.
Part B of the Schleswig-Holstein Advertisements was published twice a month (on the 15th and 30th of a month) in printed form as a justice gazette until the end of 2014. The publication of a written edition of Part B has been dispensed with since 1 January 2015. Therefore, from this date onwards, all issues of Part B (which in future will only be published once on the 30th of a month) will only be made available digitally and free of charge.

=041  \\$adut
=100  \\$aTwist, Albertus van $4aut$98813$d1696-after 1743
=245  \\$aEeuwigduurende liefdes almanak
=260  \\$aCyprus [sic]$bMirtillo$c1721
=300  \\$bengraved frontispiece and title page, leather bound, gild embossed spine, illustrations$a129 pages
=500  \\$acertainly not published in Cyprus
=500  \\$ams. note in the cover revealing Philokalus as the Leiden student Albertus van Twist
=500  \\$afrontispiece engraving depicting "La Naissance de Venus" (3 naked sea Nymphs and Venus)
=500  \\$a"Van Twist, geboren te Hulst in 1699, had zich in 1718 ingeschreven als rechtenstudent te Leiden, waar hij, als we de pamfletten mogen geloven, meer interesse toonde voor lessen in de liefde dan voor colleges. Deze pamfletten zijn blijkbaar geschreven door medestudenten of anderen die getuige waren van de pogingen tot vrijages van Van Twist. De Eeuwigduurende liefdes almanak is dus een sleutelalmanak: achter de fictieve namen in de gedichten gaan echte personen schuil. Daarmee neemt het een unieke positie in temidden van andere Nederlandse almanakken." (kb.nl)
=500  \\$aengravings on frontispiece, title-page and at pages 36, 37-59, 88, 90, 92, 94, and 122
=500  \\$aThe Eeuwigduurende liefdes almanak is one of the first almanacs that is playfully aimed by the writer and publisher who called himself by the antique name Philomúsus Philokaus, admirer of muse and beauty, and thus puts himself in the mythological tradition. This cheeky man placed elements from traditional calendars in amatory/amorous context, like the twelve months of the year of love ‘de twaelf maenden van ‘t jaer der liefde’. Visit is the first month, Hope the fifth, the eight month is called Connection, Regret the eleventh which is followed by Indifference. Also other elements of life and cycles from the year of love are described in the same style as noted above. 
=500  \\$aThe frolic author of this richly illustrated work hid his real identity behind the pseudonyms Philomúsus Philokaus and Philander Mirtillo from Cyprus (which is known as the place where the Roman goddess Venus first touched land after she was born on open sea). Revealing the person behind the almanac became an obsession short after its publication in 1721. Contemporaries tried to light the veil of mystery by spreading pamphlets. This quest ended at the student Albertus van Twist, who aimed to immortalize his impossible love for Johanna Susanna Alensoon. Van Twist, born in Hulst in 1696, registered as a law student in Leiden in 1718. If the pamphlets are right, he paid more interest about lessons of love than the actual law classes. These pamphlets are written by fellow students and other witnesses of Van Twists flirts. The Eeuwigduurende liefdes almanak is thus a key almanac, there are real people behind the fictive names in the poems, which makes this book extraordinary amid other Dutch almanacs. Besides the unusual content, there are more reasons for this book to be very special. Already in the early eighteenth century, right after publishing, this book was rare, concluding by the fact that in later years the author himself bought copies of the book. In the end everything luckily turned out well for the romantic Mister Van Twist. He promoted in 1721, the year of publishing, and moved back to Zeeuws-Vlaanderen, where he got married twice, gave life to a lot of children and finally made it to bailiff.

=500  \\$aWriter Jan de Brune (the Younger) came from an intellectual family. His works show an extensive knowledge of contemporary literature, he writes in a fresh and direct style. He only lived to be 33 years old.

=041  \\$afre$aita
=100  \\$aTasso, Torquato$d1544-1595$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q168962$94904
=245  \\$aL'Aminte
=260  \\$aThe Hague$bDyk, van$c1681
=300  \\$a[xii]186 pages$bbound in marbled cardboard, manuscript title vignet on spine, inserted illustrations, frontispiece engraving
=500  \\$aOriginally published in 1580
=500  \\$abilingual edition italian-french "Aminta, Comedia / Aminte, Comedie"
=500  \\$aAminta is a play written by Torquato Tasso in 1573, represented during a garden party at the court of Ferrara. Both the actors and the public were noble persons living at the Court, who could understand subtle allusions the poet made to that style of life, in contrast with the life of shepherds, represented in an idyllic way. The text is written in hendecasyllabic and septenary verses; it is divided into five acts. The play has a pastoral theme, and is set in the time of Alexander the Great. The characters are shepherds and nymphs.The story is about Aminta's love for the beautiful nymph Silvia, who does not return his attentions and prefers hunting. She risks rape at the hands of a Satyr but Aminta saves her; however, again she flees from him. Aminta, finding her blood-stained veil, attempts to kill himself. Now Silvia is remorseful, comes back to cry over Aminta's body who is still alive, and the two can happily marry, following the advice that older and wiser friends had been giving them.

=500  \\$aPaulus Merula, or Paul van Merle (1558-1607) was a Dutch jurist, classicist, historian, geographer and librarian. In 1592 he was appointed professor of history at Leiden University, and was elevated to full professor in 1593. From 1597 until his death he was librarian to Leiden University Library, and in 1603 he was appointed rector magnificus of the university.

=100  \\$aBaranius, August Wilhelm$4aut$98829
=245  \\$aVersuch einer Biographie der Frau Gräfin von Lichtenau
=260  \\$aZurich$aLindau$a[Leipzig]$bs.n.$c1800 [1798]
=300  \\$a[x]-132 pages
=500  \\$aWilhelmine, Gräfin von Lichtenau, born as Wilhelmine En(c)ke, also spelled Encke (1753-1820), was the official mistress of King Frederick William II of Prussia from 1769 until 1797 and was elevated by him into the nobility. She is regarded as politically active and influential in the policy of Prussia during his reign.
=500  \\$aAccording to Waltraud Maierhofer, Wilhelmine was often the subject of satire during her lifetime. This publication, actually published in Leipzig in 1798, seems to be "more a satire against enlightenment ideas than a biography". The author's name, August Wilhelm Baranius, might even be a pseudonym; Waltraud Maierhofer suggests the opera singer Henrietta Baranius (1768-1853). (Source: “Wilhelmine Encke-Ritz-Lichtenau: Writing and Reading the life of a Prussian Royal Mistress." Biography 27, no. 3 (2004): 575–96.)

=100  \\$aAnonymous$4lbt$94790
=245  \\$aLetra a la tonadilla a doce, intitulada: La Plaza de Palacio de Barcelona
=260  \\$aBarcelona$bCampins$c1774
=300  \\$a13-[2] pages$bmodern white vellum binding
=500  \\$aTonadilla was a Spanish musical song form of theatrical origin; not danced. The genre was a type of short, satirical musical comedy popular in 18th-century Spain, and later in Cuba and other Spanish colonial countries. It originated as a song type, then dialogue for characters was written into the tonadilla, and it expanded into a miniature opera lasting from 10 to 20 minutes. It drew its personages from everyday life and included popular and folk music and dance, and vernacular language. The tonadilla also influenced the development of the zarzuela, the characteristic form of Spanish musical drama or comedy. 
=500  \\$aOne of the works Valledor wrote when he was the first musician of the Barcelona Theatre
=500  \\$aNote from the antiquarian Kraus, NY "The only edition of this little tonadilla, a theatrical form which reached its apogee in the eighteenth century in the urban theatre. ... There is a list of tonadillas available from the same printer at the end of the volume...."

=500  \\$aMarmontel is a French encyclopaedist, historian, storyteller, novelist, grammarian, poet, playwright and philosopher. He was close to Voltaire in his views and was an opponent of Rousseau. Marmontel enjoyed fame throughout Europe thanks to the French court where he gained the patronage of the influential "maîtresse en titre" Madame de Pompadour in 1758, but his work was highly controversial.

=041  \\$aspa
=100  \\$aVega, Lope de$d1562-1635$4aut$98045
=245  \\$aLaurel de Apolo
=260  \\$aLondon$bLeclere$c1824
=300  \\$axvi-248 pages
=500  \\$aFélix Lope de Vega y Carpio (1562-1635) was a Spanish playwright, poet, and novelist who was a key figure in the Spanish Golden Age (1492–1659) of Baroque literature. Lope de Vega renewed the literary life of Spanish theatre when it became mass culture, and with the playwrights Pedro Calderón de la Barca and Tirso de Molina defined the characteristics of Spanish Baroque theatre with great insight into the human condition. The literary production of Lope de Vega includes 3,000 sonnets, three novels, four novellas, nine epic poems, and approximately 500 stageplays.
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1630
=648  \0$a17th Century (1601-1700)$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q7016$920923
=648  \0$a19th Century (1801-1900)$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q6955$920935

=500  \\$aChristian Friedrich Franckenstein (1621-1679) was a German teacher, classical philologist and historian.
=500  \\$aChristina (1626-1689) was a member of the House of Vasa, and the Queen of Sweden in her own right from 1632 until her abdication in 1654. The Swedish queen is remembered as one of the most learned women of the 17th century. She was fond of books, manuscripts, paintings, and sculptures. With her interest in religion, philosophy, mathematics, and alchemy, she attracted many scientists to Stockholm, wanting the city to become the "Athens of the North". The Peace of Westphalia allowed her to establish an academy or university when and wherever she wanted.

Door een van haar Staatsbedienden van tijd tot tijd versamelt, in 't Italiaansch beschreeven, nu in het Nederduitsch gebragt, met nodige figuuren en registers verrijkt.

=041  \\$aeng
=100  \\$aSwift, Jonathan$d1667-1745$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q41166$97332
=245  \\$aA Tale of a Tub
=250  \\$a9th ed.
=260  \\$aLondon$bBathurst$c1739
=300  \\$a[xxiv]-220 pages$b7 plates inserted, engraved frontispiece
=500  \\$aA 'Tale of a Tub' (see also 11A18 for the French translation) was first published by the Irish clergyman and novelist Jonathan Swift in 1704; it is the first and perhaps most difficult of all his satires. The title is thought to refer to a dissenting priest’s pulpit, and the work is a biting parody on the religious extravagances that Swift perceived among the clergy at the start of the 18th century. The narrative is written using a complex though playful technique of interlinking stories concerning the lives of three brothers, each representing one of the main branches of western Christianity. The edition is particularly noteworthy for the woodcut illustrations that punctuate the text. For example, there is a striking image of a priest reprimanding the congregation down below, with a gallows and theatre shown in the background. The frontispiece also illustrates a whale distracted by a barrel thrown overboard by sailors: an allegory, perhaps, of how the text was designed to draw the attention of political and religious dissenters away from the affairs of the ‘ship’ of state.
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1704
=590  \\$aWritten for the Universal Improvement of Mankind. To which is added, an Account of a Battle between the Antient and Modern Books in St. James's Library. (...) With the Author's Apology. And Explanatory Notes by W.W.--tt--n, B.D. and Others.

=500  \\$aoriginates from a Benectine monastery school ?
=500  \\$aEx libris "Dom Antoine Jourdez", the last Benedictine monk of Toul, who wrote a handwritten document, entitled Description of the organ, 1811 and 1813. Attached to this 422-page manuscript is a 47-page Supplement, written in 1882, by Joseph Oury, organist of Toul Cathedral. The organ of the former Saint-Étienne Cathedral of Toul (Meurthe-et-Moselle) seemed to have passed through the Revolution without incident. When the church reopened, the last of the Benedictine monks of Saint-Mansuy, Dom Antoine Jourdez, had the organ restored and assumed the position of organist until September 30, 1828.

=300  \\$a4 vols. (vi-289+263+304+316-[3] pages)
=500  \\$aAdriaan Loosjes (1761-1818) was a Dutch botanist, poet, novelist and publisher. 'Het leven van Maurits Lijnslager', a historical novel, was his best-known book.
=520  \\$aThe writer places the story around the end of the Twelve Year's Truce. Maurits Lijnslager is the son of a merchant from Amsterdam. At the age of eighteen, he must take up his father's office in Livorno. which means he would leave Rotterdam, where he met Maria van Vliet. One of her brothers becomes his traveling companion, although he soon succumbs to the miserable journey. Maurits continues his travels in the company of the Flemish painter Antonie van Dijk and meets the musician Manichetti in Florence. Together they meet the famous Galileo Galilei and Maurits becomes an eyewitness to the capture of this sage. The story also elaborates on his time in Genoa, where he meets Rubens. He declines the offer to settle there for good and travels back to the Netherlands via Switzerland. He returns from his journey with the then still youthful Milton.

=520  \\$aThe most important contemporary source on Johann Michael Haydn's life and work is the Biographical Sketch by Michael Haydn, published two years after his death by the publishing house Mayr'sche Buchhandlung in Salzburg. Published on behalf of his widow and drafted by friends of the composer: Georg Johann Schinn (1768-1833) and Joseph Otter (around 1760-1836) - both his students - as well as Haydn's "most trusted" friend, P. Werigand Rettensteiner (1751-1822) from Michaelbeuern Abbey near Salzburg.

=041  \\$alat
=100  \\$aVossius, Isaac$d1618-1689$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3112766$97742
=245  \\$aDe poematum cantu et viribus rythmi
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aOxford$bSheldonian Theatre$c1673
=300  \\$a[xii]-136 pages
=500  \\$ams. note in one copy: "v. le dict. de musique de rousseau"
=520  \\$aDe Poematum (On the Music of Poetry and Power of Rhythm)  a work of Continental musical humanism, interesting for being published in England and dedicated to royalist Henry Bennett, Duke of Arlington. This treatise plays an important but poorly understood role in the development of rhythmopoeia; Isaac Vossius continues the arguments of figures such as Vincenzo Galilei and Marin Mersenne - desiring to link linguistic rhythm, music, and the passions - by proposing a practical, if undemonstrated, method for doing so based on ancient poetic feet. This resuscitation of poetic feet in the service of affect is made explicit first by Vossius, but is undoubtedly more familiar to musicologists from Wolfgang Caspar Printz's 1696 Phrynis Mitilenaeus or Johann Mattheson's 1739 Der vollkommene Capellmeister. Vossius, or more correctly, De poematum, was often cited during the century after its publication, and no modern treatment of rhythmopoeia seems complete without a citation or very short excerpt from this work. There is little secondary literature that focuses on this treatise, but what does exist links this work directly to John Dryden's composition of his 1687 and 1697 St. Cecilia odes, and their musical settings by Giovanni Battista Draghi and Jeremiah Clarke, respectively.

=500  \\$aJan Tonnis or Theunisz (approximately 1569-1640) was a versatile figure. He was a yarn twister, book printer, bookseller, distiller, innkeeper, Arabic lecturer in Leiden and professor of Hebrew at the first 'Nederduytsche Academie' in Amsterdam. In 1639 he published 'Joseph's Droef en Bly-eynd' spel', in 3 parts; tragicomedies with allegorical characters, and with many stage performances.

=041  \\$aita$ager
=100  \\$aChristmann, Johann Friedrich$d1752-1817$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q55122884$98875
=245  \\$aCantata per il glorioso giorno del nome di sua altezza reale la Principessa Cunegonda di Sassonia
=246  \1$aFreuden-Gesang an dem glorreichen Namens-Tag ihrer Königlichen Hoheit der Durchlauchtigsten Prinzessinn Cunegunda von Sachsen
=260  \\$aSpeyer$bZumsteeg$c1790
=300  \\$a[7] pages
=500  \\$aJohann Friedrich Christmann was a German Lutheran clergyman, composer of church songs and chamber music, pianist, flautist and music theorist. He studied in Tübingen from 1770, and after two years became an apostolic vicariate. He worked as a tutor in 1777 in Winterthur (Switzerland) and in 1780 in Karlsruhe. In 1783 or 1784 he was appointed minister of Heutingsheim, where he worked for the rest of his life.
=500  \\$aMaria Kunigunde von Sachsen (1740-1826) had sung in Hasse's Leucippo but eventually, in 1775, became abbess (coadjutor) of Essen and Thorn. She remained influential at the court of her brother Wenceslas in Koblenz, Elector of Trier.

=100  \\$aWyten, Gerard$4aut$98876
=245  \\$aHet Houweliick van de Herderinne Roseliine ende den Herder Thiter
=260  \\$aLeiden$bvander Boxe$c1650
=300  \\$a83-[1] pages
=500  \\$aGerard Wyten lived in Soetermeer in the middle of the seventeenth century. He was a friend of Jacob Cats, and wrote verses along the lines of Cats. Three works by him are known, all printed in Leiden in 1650, which bear the title: 'Den Lof van de Herderinne Roselijne, haer toegeschreven van den Herder Thiter, enz. gedeeltelijk in proza, gedeeltelijk in verzen'; 'Hemelschen Minnebrief, gesonden aen de Herderinne Roselijne van den Herder Thiter geheel in verzen' and this publication 'Het Houwelijck van Herderinne Roselijne en den Herder Thiter, gegrond op Gods Eere, ende de bevorderinge van haerder beyder Salichheyt, mede in verzen'.

=041  \\$adut$hspa
=245  \\$aDen geheymen minnaar.$bBlyspel
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bvan Goedesberg$c1655
=300  \\$a[64] pages$bengraved frontispiece
=500  \\$aCatharina Questiers (1631-1669) was a seventeenth-century poet and playwright. Together with Cornelia van der Veer (1639-?) and Katharyne Lescailje (1649-1711), she is considered one of the best-known and most successful poets of the second half of the seventeenth century. She also made her own engravings, accompanying her publications.
=500  \\$aBetween 1654 and 1663, her poems appeared in various anthologies. She also wrote three prose translations of Spanish plays. All three of these comedies were performed in the Amsterdam Schouwburg. 'Den geheymen minnaar' was the first play; 'Casimier of gedempte hoogmoet' the second, which was performed by Ariana Nozeman, the first female professional actor; and the third one 'd’Ondanckbare Fulvius en trouwe Octavia' was used for the opening of the new theatre in 1665.
=500  \\$a'Den geheymen minnaar' was dedicated to Queen Christina of Sweden
=500  \\$aContains laudatory poems by Dirk Kalbergen, Jan van Dalen, J. Koenerding
=500  \\$aFélix Lope de Vega y Carpio (1562-1635) was a celebrated playwright and poet. He is considered emblematic of the Golden Age of Spanish literature and one of the most prolific authors in world literature.
=500  \\$aThe title of Lope de Vega's play 'Amor secreto hasta celos' is written in ink on the title page (by a previous owner), while Questiers' adaptation is actually based on his 'Si no vieran las mujeres'. 
=561  \\$aEx libris E. Günthner (manuscript)

=500  \\$aDuring his lifetime, Gumpelzhaimer was best known for this 'Compendium musicæ', a method addressed to his students and enjoying thirteen editions up until 1681. The last edition revised by the author is the 8th, from 1625. It is inspired by the 'Compendiolum musicæ' published by Heinrich Faber in 1548 and its translation, which Gumpelzhaimer expanded with numerous musical examples.

=100  \\$aPascal, Blaise$d1623-1662$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1290$98885
=245  \\$aPensées ... sur la religion et sur quelques autres sujets
=250  \\$aRev. ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bMortier$c1750
=300  \\$a50-[50]-266-[14]-128 pages
=500  \\$aThe Pensées (Thoughts) is a collection of fragments written by the French 17th-century philosopher and mathematician Blaise Pascal. Pascal's religious conversion led him into a life of asceticism, and the Pensées was in many ways his life's work. It represented Pascal's defense of the Christian religion, and the concept of "Pascal's wager" stems from a portion of this work.
=500  \\$aPascal's wager is a philosophical argument postulating that individuals essentially engage in a life-defining gamble regarding the belief in the existence of God.
=590  \\$aAugmentée de beaucoup de pensées, de la vie de l'autheur, & de quelques dissertations.

=250  \\$a2nd ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bLibraires associés$c1796
=300  \\$a2 vols. in 1 (viii-215-[iv]-220-xviii pages)
=500  \\$aDupaty was a French magistrate, criminal law reformer and man of letters. He was chamber president of the parliament of Bordeaux and made his mark in several causes célèbres.
=500  \\$aOriginally published posthumously in 2 parts in 1789, which met with great success and was translated into German, English and Russian. Rome placed it on the Index librorum prohibitorum. Dupaty is above all a gentleman thrown on the Grand Tour. However, rather than describing the ruins of an extinct star in a soothing manner, he focuses on the men - especially the women - and their customs: death, misery, and toil.These letters are epistolary in name only, since they were written for the sole purpose of publication. 
=500  \\$athe 'Lettres sur l'Italie' were on the Index librorum prohibitorum

=500  \\$aAntoinette Du Ligier de la Garde Deshoulières (1638-1694) was a French poet. She had a good education; she had acquiried a knowledge of Latin, Spanish and Italian, and studied prosody under the direction of the poet Jean Hesnault. Her daughter, Antoinette-Thérèse Deshoulières (1659-1718), inherited her wit and talent for writing.

=041  \\$agrc$alat
=245  \\$a[New Testament]
=250  \\$a1st ed.?
=260  \\$a[Paris]$bEstienne$c[1546]
=300  \\$a528-362 pages$bsmall
=500  \\$aRobert I Estienne (1503-1559), known as Robertus Stephanus in Latin and sometimes referred to as Robert Stephens, was a 16th-century printer in Paris. He was the proprietor of the Estienne print shop after the death of his father Henri Estienne, the founder of the Estienne printing firm. Estienne published and republished many classical texts as well as Greek and Latin translations of the Bible.
=500  \\$atitle page and last couple pages are missing; could be the first edition from 1546 (being Estienne's first Greek new testament).
=500  \\$a"This 1546 edition is also known as the 'O mirifica' edition, from Estienne's preface beginning "O mirificam Regis nostri optimi & prestantissimi principis liberalitatem", in which the printer praises the King for commissioning Claude Garamond to create a new Greek font in order to produce volumes in small format. Robert Estienne based the text on a comparison of the Complutense and the Erasmian editions with sixteen manuscripts. This collation was made by Robert Estienne's own son, Henri." (https://www.lux-et-umbra.com/descriptions/nt.php)

=500  \\$aModeled after the French 'Almanach des Muses' (see 09A29, 11A07 and 1B19), the 'Musen-Almanach' was founded in Göttingen in 1770 (see H1-019-20)

=100  \\$aSweerts, Cornelis$d1669-1742$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2311859$98901
=245  \\$aLeerzaame fabelen
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bStrander$c1704
=300  \\$a[xii]-128-[4] pages$billustrations
=500  \\$aCornelis Sweerts (1669-1749) was a poet, songwriter, playwright and bookseller. His 'Inleiding tot de zang- en speelkunst' describes musical life in Amsterdam at the end of the 17th century. In it, he makes a plea for writing in the Dutch language and composing on Dutch texts (in reaction to French and Italian).
=500  \\$aTogether with Abraham Alewijn he is considered to be among the two most important songwriters of his time. They published a total of eight songbooks, which were reprinted many times. Their song texts were set to music mainly by the composers David Petersen, Nicolaas Ferdinand le Grand, Hendrik Anders and Servaes de Koninck.

=008  220818s1767\\\\||||||||\||||\00|\0\fre\d
=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aPinot Duclos, Charles$d1704-1772$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q982034$98370
=245  \\$aConsidérations sur les mœurs de ce siècle
=250  \\$a5th ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bPrault; Durand$c1767
=300  \\$a[vi]-iv-484-[6] pages$btitle page in red and black ink, engraved title page
=500  \\$aOriginally published in 1751
=500  \\$aDuclos's 'Considérations sur les moeurs de ce siècle' of 1751, has been undeservedly neglected in recent times, despite being lauded as a masterpiece by critics of its day. Mistakenly read by many as a succession of maxims in the tradition of La Rochefoucauld and La Bruyère, Duclos's sixteen essays on subjects ranging from education, manners and wit to reputation, virtue and honour in fact break with the universalizing tones of the genre, attacking the shallow values of court culture and the aristocracy, while promoting in their place a 'morale de l'utile'. Prefiguring Jeremy Bentham's utilitarianism, Les Considérations argue that the public good and the happiness of the greatest number are the only sensible criteria for determining the conduct of individuals and institutions. The subject-matter of the essays reflects the dominant preoccupations of eighteenth-century French court society: outward show and standing in the eyes of others, so exquisitely satirized in Patrice Leconte's 1996 film Ridicule. The tyranny of fashion and wit, and the fear of mockery, are thus the central targets of these pithy and entertainingly written pieces. In essence, Duclos champions what he calls 'le prix réel des choses', to which he devotes an entire chapter, inspired by Pufendorf's 'Le Droit de la nature et des gens'. 
=504  \\$ahttps://www.persee.fr/doc/dhs_0070-6760_1996_num_28_1_2126

=041  \\$ager
=100  \\$aLübbecke, Fried$d1883-1965$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1456304$98922
=245  \\$aFrankfurt am Main: Goethes Heimat
=260  \\$aFrankfurt am Main$bKramer$c1946
=300  \\$a59 pages$bcolour photographs
=500  \\$aThe Goethe House is a writer's house museum located in the Innenstadt district of Frankfurt am Main, Germany. It is the birthplace and childhood home of German poet and playwright Johann Wolfgang von Goethe. It is also the place where Goethe wrote his famous works Götz von Berlichingen, The Sorrows of Young Werther, and the first drafts of Urfaust. The house has mostly been operated as a museum since its 1863 purchase by the Freies Deutsches Hochstift (Free German Foundation), displaying period furniture and paintings from Goethe's time in the house.
The Goethe House was destroyed by Allied bombing in World War II, but reconstructed afterwards. It is located adjacent to the Deutsches Romantik-Museum, which opened in 2021.

=100  1\$aHaller, Albrecht von$d1708-1777$4edt$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q123225$98927
=245  \\$aGöttingische Zeitungen von gelehrten Sachen auf das Jahr MDCCLI$nnos. 1-7, 11-114, 117-124, 127-128
=260  \\$aGöttingen$bSchmid$c1751
=300  \\$a[vi]-1296-[40] pages
=500  \\$aThe Göttingische Gelehrten Anzeigen is considered as the oldest scholarly journal still published in the German-speaking world. In this specialised journal, scholars critically review contemporary scientific works. The first volume was published in 1739 under the title Göttingische Zeitung(en) von gelehrten Sachen, from 1747 under the direction of the physician Albrecht von Haller. From 1753, the journal was published by the Göttingen Academy of Sciences and Humanities, which was founded in 1751, and was called Göttingische Anzeigen von gelehrten Sachen until 1801. The current title was introduced in 1802; since then the journal has been published by Vandenhoeck & Ruprecht, with the exception of the years 1896 to 1935, when it was published by the Berlin publishing house Weidmann. There were only interruptions between 1944 and 1953, as well as in 1960 and 1961.

=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bMortier$c1716
=300  \\$a[xii]-241-[3] pages$bleather bound, decorated endpapers, marbled edges, engraved title page
=500  \\$aCaptivi is a Latin play by the early Roman playwright Titus Maccius Plautus, written circa 200 BCE. The title has been translated as The Captives or The Prisoners, and the plot focuses on slavery and prisoners of war. Although the play contains much broad humor, it is a relatively serious treatment of significant themes compared to most of Plautus’ other comedies.

=100  \\$aPompeius Trogus, Gnæus$cPompey Trogue$4aut$98939
=245  \\$aIustini historiarum ex Trogo Pompeio lib. XLIV cum notis Isaaci Vossii
=260  \\$aLeiden$bElsevier$c1640
=300  \\$a[xiv]-294+39-[54] pages
=500  \\$aGnaeus Pompeius Trogus' principal work was his 44-volume Philippic Histories and the Origin of the Whole World and the Places of the Earth (Historiae Philippicae et Totius Mundi Origines et Terrae Situs), now lost, which, according to its surviving epitome, had as its principal theme the Macedonian Empire founded by Philip II but functioned as a general history of all of the parts of the world which fell under the control of Alexander the Great and his successors, with extensive ethnographical and geographical digressions.
=500  \\$aThe original text of the Philippic Histories has been lost and is preserved only in excerpts by other authors (including Vopiscus, Jerome, and Augustine) and in a loose epitome by the later historian Justin (Marcus Junianus Justinus Frontinus). Justin aimed only to preserve the parts he felt most important or interesting about Pompeius Trogus's work, with the last recorded event being the recovery of Roman standards from the Parthians in 20 BC. In the manuscripts of Justin's works, however, a separate series of summaries (prologi) of the original work have been preserved.

=500  \\$aLetters from a Peruvian Woman is a 1747 epistolary novel. It tells the story of Zilia, a young Incan princess, who is abducted from the Temple of the Sun by the Spanish during the Spanish conquest of the Inca Empire. In a series of letters to her fiancé Aza, who is also the Sapa Inca, Zilia tells the story of her capture, her rescue by French sailors, her befriending of the captain Déterville and her introduction to French society.

=500  \\$aFüssli the Elder was a Swiss painter and writer. He is the founder of Swiss art history. =100  \\$aRapin, René$d1621-1687$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q511359$4aut$98942
=245  \\$aLes Œuvres diverses$n3/4
=246  \1$aOeuvres diverses touchant la réligion
=250  \\$a2nd ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bRoger$c1710
=300  \\$a552-[6] pages$btitle page in red and black ink, leather bound, embossed gilded spine, marbled endpapers
=500  \\$aRené Rapin (1621–1687) was a French Jesuit and writer. He taught rhetoric, and wrote extensively both in verse and prose. 
=500  \\$aThe first essay, L'esprit du christianisme, is dedicated to the not named "abbess" of the Royal Abbey of Our Lady of Fontevraud or Fontevrault, a monastery in the village of Fontevraud-l'Abbaye, near Chinon, in the former French duchy of Anjou. The abbesess during Rapin's lifetime were Jeanne-Baptiste de Bourbon (1637–1670) and Gabrielle de Rochechouart de Mortemart (1670–1704).
=500  \\$aFIrst published in 1693
=500  \\$aRapin was, amongst other, the author of several theological and ascetic treatises like De nova doctrina dissertatio seu Evangelium Jansenistarum (Paris, 1656), L'esprit du christianisme (Paris, 1672), La perfection du christianisme (Paris, 1673), La foi des derniers siècles (Paris, 1679). These books and many other pamphlets were collected in Oeuvres complétes published at Amsterdam, 1709–10, a compilation of various works by the author, including poems, essays and speeches. The subjects covered in the book are varied, ranging from politics and religion to literature and philosophy. Rapin's writings are known for their elegant style and erudite content. Les Oeuvres Diverses is considered an important work of eighteenth-century French literature.

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aGrignion de Montfort, Louis-Marie$d1673-1716$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q88927$4aut$98943
=245  \\$aCantiques des missions
=260  \\$aPoitiers$bFaulcon$c1779
=300  \\$a258-[3] pages$bleather bound, embossed gilded spine
=500  \\$aLouis-Marie Grignion de Montfort was a French Catholic priest known for his preaching and his influence on Mariology. He was made a missionary apostolic by Pope Clement XI. Montfort wrote a number of books which went on to become classic Catholic titles and influenced several popes.
=500  \\$aWhile Montfort is best known for his spiritual writings, he was also a poet and during his missions managed to compose more than 20,000 verses of hymns. His hymns and canticles were, for the most part, meant to be sung in village churches and in the homes of the poor. Based on the analysis of Bishop Hendrik Frehen of the Company of Mary, Montfortian hymns fall into two major categories: "inspired" and "didactic." The inspired canticles flow spontaneously, on the occasion of a pilgrimage to a Marian shrine, or on the occasion of a joyful celebration. The didactic hymns took more effort and time to compose, and focus on instructional and informative qualities: they teach the audience through the use of a moral and a theme. After Montfort's death, the Company of Mary (which continued his work of preaching parish renewals) made great use of his hymns and used them as instruments of evangelization.

=100  \\$aCarion, Johann$d1499-1537$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q92506$4aut$98944
=245  \\$aMathematici chronicorum libri tres
=260  \\$aParis$bMaceus$c1557
=300  \\$a[130]-619-[26] pages$bbound in leather, gilt decorations on back, marbled endpapers, (red) drawn margin lines on pages $c8vo
=500  \\$aJohannes Carion was a German astrologer, historian and mathematician. 
=500  \\$aCarion's Chronicles became an important work in Lutheran and more generally Protestant millenarian thought. From an original that was indeed penned by Carion, it was completely rewritten in its Latin version at the hands of Melanchthon, and others. With Joachim Camerarius, Melanchthon and other Lutheran humanist scholars the work changed from a traditional chronicle into a Reformation narrative of the Middle Ages. After Melanchthon's death, Caspar Peucer continued to edit it. Major features were the scheme of four monarchies taken from the Book of Daniel, extended by the medieval idea of translatio imperii; further there is a second Three Eras schematic, the third period of which will be co-extensive with the Roman Empire extended by the Holy Roman Empire (the fourth monarchy) which will last to 2000 AD.
https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Carion

=500  \\$aAbove the text is written: "de la part de Blanchet, Elêve et successeur de P. Taskin"; Below the text is printed: "Au Louvre, le 13 décembre 1788. =520  \\$aBlanchet was a pupil of Taskin, but Taskin was also pupil of Blanchet. François-Étienne Blanchet II (c. 1730-1766) was François-Étienne Blanchet I's son and like him became a harpsichord maker, learning from his father. Pascal Taskin became his apprentice and took over his workshop after his early death. Armand-François-Nicolas Blanchet (1763-1818) was the son of François-Étienne Blanchet II and brought up and trained by Pascal Taskin after his father's early death.

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aQuétant, François-Antoine$d1733-1823$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q21535099$4lbt$98949
=245  \\$aLe Serrurier$bOpera Buffon; Essai sur l'Opéra-Comique
=260  \\$aParis$bDuchesne$c1766
=300  \\$a31 pages$bno cover
=500  \\$a'Le Serrurier' (The Locksmith) is a one-act comic opera based on a drama by M. de La Ribardière. It premiered on 20 December 1764 at the Comédie-Italienne in Paris, at the Hôtel de Bourgogne. The information in the printed libretto indicates that before the performance at the Comédie-Italienne, the work was performed privately at the home of Prince Conti and was also dedicated to him. In total, it was performed 34 times at the Comédie-Italienne; although most of the performances date from 1764-1769, it was still being performed in 1779.
=500  \\$aThe score of Le Serrurier (https://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k1163875g/f5.item) was published in its time and therefore - unlike many of Kohaut's other works - survived. In addition, numerous melodies from it were also published in contemporary collections of arias, which, along with the number of performances at the Comédie-Italienne and documented productions at other theatres, attest to the popularity of the piece at the time. 'Le Serrurier' was created in a time that the genre of opéra comique was undergoing a significant transformation: while performances with pre-existing and re-textured music ("vaudeville") had prevailed, "ariettes", melodies written specifically for comic operas, began to penetrate comic operas, and from the turn of the 1750s onwards, "ariettes" were written for comic operas. Among the early examples of this kind is Kohaut's The Locksmith. Interestingly, Quétant himself, the author of the libretto, theorized on the issue - among other things in a special treatise accompanying the printed libretto of The Locksmith, entitled 'Essai sur 'opera comique' - and preferred vaudeville to "true" comic opera
=500  \\$aJosef Kohaut was born into a czech musical family: his father was an organist in Saaz (today Žatec). He was a troupe trumpeter in the Austrian army, but defected to France, where he was known as composer and lutenist in the chapel of Louis-François de Bourbon, Prince de Conti, where he was engaged. In this capacity, he wrote a number of operas for the Comédie Italienne, and sonatas for harpsichord. His greatest success was Le Serrurier, since it is cited five years after its premiere on December 20, 1764, and the libretto has been translated into German, Dutch, Czech and Swedish.
=504  \\$aCzech wikipedia article about this opera:
https://cs.wikipedia.org/wiki/Z%C3%A1me%C4%8Dn%C3%ADk_(opera)

He became director of the music-school Leipzig, including directing the Thomanerchor at the Thomaskirche. =300  \\$a[ii]-440 pages$bmusic examples
=500  \\$aSee 04E01 for the 3rd revised (1847) edition and 02B19 for an Italian translation
=500  \\$aThe preface is missing, but is reproduced in 04E01. In the preface to the third edition, Fétis informs us that he finished writing this edition in early 1833, at which moment he moved to Brussels to become royal chapel master and director to the Brussels Conservatoire. The new job delayed the publication until 1834. This edition was printed in the "nombre énorme de quatre mille exemplaires" and was translated into Spanish, English (with reprint in Boston), and Russian.

This metrical psalter, a translation of the Genevan Psalter, became one of the standard psalm-books used by the evangelical churches of the German-speaking lands

=100  \\$aBraunschweig-Lüneburg, Sophie Elisabeth von$d1613-1676$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q448131$98975
=245  \\$aChrist Fürstliches Davids-Harpfen-Spiel
=260  \\$aNuremberg$bGerhard$c1667
=300  \\$a[xxx]-265-[5] pages
=500  \\$aHyms and devotional arias
=500  \\$aSophie Elisabeth von Braunschweig-Lüneburg was a German poet, composer and impressario, and by marriage Duchess of Brunswick-Lüneburg. Most of Elisabeth Sophie 's compositions are hymns or devotional arias. Some of these were published in 1651 and 1667. The one printed in 1651, Vinetum evangelicum, Evangelischer Weinberg, is believed to have been the first music published by a woman in Germany. Her stephson Anton Ulrich was a patron of the arts, a writer, an art collector and one of the main proponents of enlightened absolutism among the Brunswick dukes.

=245  \\$aProcessionale ad usum sacri, et canonici Præmonstratensis$bordinis reverendissimi in Christo Patris Domini
=260  \\$aParis$bLeonard$c1666
=300  \\$a[viii]-424-lxxxxix-[8] pages$bmetal locks, red edges, embossed leather cover
=500  \\$a1645-1666 : Augustin Ier Le Scellier was abbot of the Prémontré Abbey , the mother house of the Premonstratensian Order, located at Prémontré about twelve miles west of Laon, département of Aisne, France. The Order of Canons Regular of Prémontré (Latin: Candidus et Canonicus Ordo Praemonstratensis), also known as the Norbertines is a religious order of canons regular of the Catholic Church founded in Prémontré near Laon in 1120 by Norbert of Xanten, who later became Archbishop of Magdeburg. Premonstratensians are designated by O.Praem. (Ordo Praemonstratensis) following their name.

=100  \\$aBeronicius, Petrus Johannes$4aut$98983
=245  \\$aBoeren- en overheids-strijd,$bofte Het verooverde Middelburg
=246  \1$aBeronicii Poemata
=246  \1$aBoeren en overheidsstrijd door Beronicius beschreven
=246  \1$aDe Weergaloze Dichter P. J. Beronicius, ten deele Voor de Nederduitsche vertaalt$bMet een bijvoegsel in de voorreden van 's mans leven
=246  \1$aP. J. Beronicii Poëta Incomparabilis Quae P. Rabus recensuit, & Georgarchontomachiae notas addidit, infertis anonymi, cujusdam commentariolis, quibus nomina propria & difficiliora quaedem explicantur
=250  \\$a3rd ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bten Hoorn$c1702
=300  \\$a[xxxii]-173 pages$bengraved frontispiece, inserted ingravings
=500  \\$aOriginally published as 'Georgarchontomachia' (1691)
=500  \\$aP.J. Beronicius is probably a mystification; the real author might be Dirk Buysero Dutch librettist, playwright and poet (1644-1708)?
=500  \\$aBeronicius (fl. 1650) was a mysterious character, possibly a monk who had eloped, a talented eccentric, who in the 17th century wandered through France, England and the Netherlands and spent a long time in Zeeland. He earned his living by sweeping chimneys, was often inebriated and drowned in a street gutter in such a state. Apart from modern languages, he mastered ancient languages with great virtuosity, spoke and wrote poetry in Latin and Greek. The most prominent of his poems is this burlesque comic-heroic poem in Latin hexameters about the raid of the Walchers in Middelburg in 1672.
=501  \\$aBound in with Dousa's 'Poemata' and engravings after Caspar Luyken, Dutch engraver and draughtsman (1672-1708)
=590  \\$aIn twee boeken. Heldendicht uit de vuist weg geschreven door N. een ooggetuige . Met vrijen trant vertaald / Libre duo. Carmine epico extemporaneo conscripti. Auctore N. Autopte
=648  \0$a17th Century (1601-1700)$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q7016$920923

=650  \0$aComedy$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q40831$921436

=500  \\$aJohan van Oldenbarnevelt, Heer van Berkel en Rodenrijs, Gunterstein and Bakkum, played an important role in the Dutch struggle for independence from Spain and was executed in 1619
=500  \\$athe first pages of the book block are heavily affected by book worm
=500  \\$aEssay about the book and the editions by Robert Fruin (1903): https://www.dbnl.org/tekst/frui001vers08_01/frui001vers08_01_0030.php. The publishers name, Jan Heindrikze, could be a pseudonym for Josua Van Der Straten, whose 1669 edition didn't sell as much because of another, more elaborate one in 1670 by Johannes Naeranus. 
Naeranus commented heavily on Van der Stratens edition; the Heindrikze edition also contains this commentary. 
This theory presents this edition as an attempt of Van der Straten to recycle a part of his earlier print.

=041  \\$ager
=100  \\$aAdolph, Paul$d1868-1941 $1https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q112983$99046
=245  \\$aVom Hof- zum Staatstheater.$bZwei Jahrzehnte persönlicher Erinnerungen an Sachsens Hoftheater, Königshaus Staatstheater und anderes
=260  \\$c1932$aDresden$bHeinrich
=300  \\$avii-506 pages
=500  \\$aIn 1909 Adolph was appointed a collegiate member of the general management of the Royal Saxon Court Theatre. He took part in the First World War as a war volunteer and served in the 1st Uhlan Regiment No. 17 in Oschatz. After Paul Adolph had worked for eleven years in the general management (including his last position as administrative director) at the Saxon Court Theatre and then in the Saxon Ministries of Culture, the Interior and Justice, he became general director of the Saxon State Theatre after the National Socialist ‘seizure of power’ in March 1933. He held this position until 1935. He died two days before reaching the age of 73 and was buried in the Trinitatisfriedhof cemetery in Dresden, where his tomb can still be found today.
=500  \\$aThe Königliche Hoftheater Dresden (also known as the Altes Hoftheater) was the predecessor of today's Semperoper, which served as a theatre for opera and drama in the royal Saxon residence city of Dresden between 1841 and 1869.
